Path splicing enables flexible, reliable routing by combining multiple routing trees ("slices") over a single topology, with contributions from authors like Neil Spring, Hari Balakrishnan, and others, enhancing dynamic path switching, low latency, and high reliability in intra- and interdomain scenarios.
This paper on Route Redistribution (RR) involves authors like Anirudh Ramachandran, Stefan Savage, and others, highlighting its complexity and need for improved routing safety.
The paper proposes **PLayer**, a policy-aware switching layer for data centers, with contributions from authors like Martin Karsten, Amin Vahdat, and others, focusing on efficient traffic routing, flexibility, and resource efficiency under network changes.
The paper proposes a cost-effective, high-bandwidth data center network architecture using commodity Ethernet switches, with contributions from authors like Alexandre Proutiere, T. S. Eugene Ng, and others, focusing on full aggregate bandwidth without hardware or software modifications.
The paper presents **DCell**, a scalable, fault-tolerant, and high-capacity recursive network structure for data centers, with contributions from authors like Alan Demers, Qiang Zhang, Shouyuan Chen, Jennifer Rexford, and others, enhancing its credibility and impact.
The paper presents **eXpose**, a novel statistical rule mining technique for network traffic analysis, co-authored by experts like Mayank Jain, Lionel M. Ni, and others, focusing on communication patterns, network monitoring, and intrusion detection.

The paper introduces *shadow configurations*, a novel approach for pre-deployment evaluation of network configurations, with contributions from notable authors like Abraham Silberschatz, Yu Wang, and Jennifer Rexford, focusing on reducing errors and disruptions efficiently.
The paper, co-authored by experts like Dushyanth Narayanan, M. Frans Kaashoek, and Ion Stoica, proposes an enterprise network architecture where hosts use *network exception handlers* to enhance efficiency and performance by leveraging exposed network state.
The paper, co-authored by experts like Heejo Lee, Randy H. Katz, and Vyas Sekar, demonstrates SampleWidth, an algorithm optimizing channel width in wireless systems for improved throughput, range, and power efficiency.
SWIFT is a wideband system that coexists with narrowband devices by dynamically aggregating non-contiguous unused frequency bands, achieving higher throughput and range while maintaining narrowband-friendly operation, with contributions from authors like Jinyang Li, Vishal Misra, Bruce Maggs, and others.
ZigZag is an 802.11 receiver design that decodes colliding packets by leveraging interference-free segments, with contributions from authors like Lionel M. Ni, Alex C. Snoeren, and Shyamnath Gollakota, focusing on near-zero packet loss without MAC modifications.
The paper presents AutoRE, a spam detection framework identifying 7,721 campaigns and 340,050 botnet IPs, with contributions from authors like Daekyeong Moon, Aleksandar Kuzmanovi, and others in fields like data mining and network security.
The paper presents a Time Machine (TM) system for network traffic archiving and retrieval, integrating intrusion detection for forensics, with contributions from authors like Guang Yao, Kang G. Shin, and Li Zhang, among others, demonstrating high-volume effectiveness.
The paper presents StopIt, a DoS defense system with a closed-control, open-service architecture, developed by authors including David Wetherall, Yih-Chun Hu, and Michael Walfish, which blocks attack traffic from millions of bots within minutes and outperforms existing systems in most scenarios, except for link-congestion attacks where capability-based systems are better.
The paper proposes an augmented DFA model with auxiliary variables and optimization techniques to mitigate state-space explosion, significantly reducing memory, runtime, and per-flow state while maintaining high-speed performance for deep packet inspection, with contributions from authors like Konstantina Papagiannaki, Sailesh Kumar, Graham Cormode, and others.

The paper proposes IMMC, a supervised subspace learning algorithm for streaming data, with contributions from authors like D. W. Embley, Xiaoli Li, and others, focusing on incremental optimization of Maximum Margin Criterion.
The central paper "2PXMiner" is authored by prominent researchers including Ying Wu, Osmar R. Zaïane, Kian-Lee Tan, Elke A. Rundensteiner, Jiawei Han, and others, focusing on efficient XML query pattern mining with enhanced performance and scalability.
The paper proposes an efficient redundancy-based feature selection method for microarray data, collaborating with authors like Jing Li, Jun Liu, and Tanya Y. Berger-Wolf, to improve classification accuracy by removing redundant genes while maintaining discriminative power.
The paper proposes a cross-collection mixture model for comparative text mining (CTM) to analyze themes across text collections, with contributions from authors like Dafna Shahaf, Xuerui Wang, and Andrew McCallum, demonstrating effectiveness in news and product reviews.
The paper proposes a data mining approach using visual dictionaries, classification trees, and an α-Semantics Graph for improved image retrieval, with contributions from authors like Richard F. Helm, Wei-Ying Ma, and others in semantic modeling and efficiency.
The paper proposes a DEA-based method for combining classifiers, with contributions from authors like Shane Butler, Bing Liu, and Geoffrey I. Webb, demonstrating equivalence to ROC analysis for 2-class problems and superior performance for k-class problems.
The paper proposes a framework for optimal randomization schemes in privacy-preserving data mining using mixture models, with contributions from authors like Johannes Gehrke, Lei Liu, and Rakesh Agrawal, balancing performance, mutual information loss, and privacy metrics.
The paper proposes a reinforcement learning-based MDP framework for cross-channel marketing optimization, validated with a 7-8% profit increase at Saks Fifth Avenue, with contributions from authors like Bing Liu, Aurelie C. Lozano, and Vipin Kumar.
The paper presents an interactive system using decision tree classifiers for land cover modeling and remote sensing image mining, integrating spectral, DEM, and GIS data, with contributions from authors like Selim Aksoy, Raghu Ramakrishnan, and Jaiwei Han.
The paper, co-authored by experts like Andrew Tomkins, Eva Tardos, and Jure Leskovec, proposes cross-post network analysis for Usenet newsgroups, revealing small-world properties and introducing spectral clustering for topical classification.
The paper discusses efficient feature selection methods for high-dimensional scientific datasets, with contributions from authors Shawn Newsam, Chandrika Kamath, Ramdev Kanapady, Aleksandar Lazarevic, and Erick Cantu-Paz, covering challenges and strategies in astronomy, plasma physics, and remote sensing.
The paper proposes a general ensemble method incorporating data quality matrices to enhance predictive accuracy by reducing variance, with contributions from authors like Philip Yu, Deepayan Chakrabarti, and others.
The paper presents an automated two-step system for mapping supplier part numbers to internal part numbers in BOMs, with contributions from authors like Oivind Johnsen, Haibin Cheng, Yan Liu, and others, enhancing efficiency over manual processes.
The paper proposes a real-time topic trend analysis framework using a dynamically learned finite mixture model, with contributions from authors like Matthias Schubert, Hans-Peter Kriegel, Philip Yu, and Vipin Kumar, focusing on topic structures, emerging topics, and characterization, demonstrated on help desk data.
The paper proposes a travel time prediction method using probe-car data with AR and state space models, validated by Nagoya data, and authored by experts including Yuko Maruyama, Christos Faloutsos, and Kenji Yamanishi.
The paper demonstrates efficient SQL implementation of K-means clustering with optimizations for Euclidean distance, nearest-cluster queries, and indexing, co-authored by experts including Ramakrishnan, Yu, and Aggarwal.
The paper explores heuristic document preprocessing techniques (IDF, normalization, log transformations) to enhance naive Bayes and multinomial mixture clustering, with contributions from authors like Ramnath Balasubramanyan, Byron Dom, and Raghu Ramakrishnan.
The paper explores machine learning methods (random forests, SVMs) for disease classification using metabolomic data, with contributions from authors like Chris Beecher, Jerome P. Reiter, and Ashish P. Sanil, addressing data challenges and biochemical insights.
The paper introduces Analytical View (AV) in MBF for OLTP-OLAP integration, with contributions from authors Jonathan Tang, Sam Skrivan, Youxuan Jin, and Adam Yeh.
